2.14 The Harmonic Mean

The Harmonic Mean (HM) is a type of average that is particularly useful for data sets consisting of rates, speeds, or ratios, especially when the numerator (e.g., distance in speed, amount of work in rates) is constant.

Definition for Ungrouped Data:

For a set of \(n\) non-zero values \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_n\), the harmonic mean (denoted as \(H\)) is defined as the reciprocal of the arithmetic mean of the reciprocals of those values:

\[H = \frac{n}{\frac{1}{x_1} + \frac{1}{x_2} + \ldots + \frac{1}{x_n}} = \frac{n}{\sum_{i=1}^{n} \frac{1}{x_i}} \quad (\text{where } x_i \ne 0)\]

Application and Example:

The harmonic mean is the appropriate average to use when rates are expressed as "x per y" and the quantity "x" is constant. Conversely, if "y" is constant, the arithmetic mean is typically more suitable. Consider an example: A car travels the first 30 km at 15 km/hr, the second 30 km at 20 km/hr, and the third 30 km at 25 km/hr. Since the distance (numerator) for each segment is constant (30 km), the harmonic mean is the correct average to find the overall average speed.

In this scenario, the harmonic mean is calculated as:

\[H = \frac{3}{\frac{1}{15} + \frac{1}{20} + \frac{1}{25}}\]
\[H = \frac{3}{\left(\frac{4+3}{60}\right) + \frac{1}{25}} = \frac{3}{\frac{7}{60} + \frac{1}{25}} = \frac{3}{\frac{35+12}{300}} = \frac{3}{\frac{47}{300}}\]
\[H = \frac{3 \times 300}{47} = \frac{900}{47} \approx 19.15 \text{ km/hr}\]

This result represents the average speed over the entire journey.

Definition for Grouped Frequency Distributions:

For data organized into a grouped frequency distribution with \(k\) classes, having class marks \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_k\) and corresponding frequencies \(f_1, f_2, \ldots, f_k\) (where \(n = \sum_{i=1}^{k} f_i\) is the total number of observations), the harmonic mean is given by:

\[H = \frac{n}{\frac{f_1}{x_1} + \frac{f_2}{x_2} + \ldots + \frac{f_k}{x_k}} = \frac{n}{\sum_{i=1}^{k} \frac{f_i}{x_i}}\]

Weighted Harmonic Mean:

For a set of values \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_k\) with respective weights \(w_1, w_2, \ldots, w_k\), the weighted harmonic mean (\(H_w\)) is defined as:

\[H_w = \frac{\sum_{i=1}^{k} w_i}{\sum_{i=1}^{k} \frac{w_i}{x_i}}\]

Example 3.9a: Average Rate of Water Flow from Various Irrigation Methods in Haryana

Find the harmonic mean of the rate of water flow (liters/minute) from various irrigation methods used by farmers in Haryana.

Flow Rate (liters/min) 50-100 100-150 150-200 200-250 250-300 300-350 350-400
Number of Fields (f) 9 10 17 10 5 4 5

Solution:

We calculate the harmonic mean below:

Flow Rate (liters/min) \(x_i\) \(f_i\) \(\frac{1}{x_i}\) \(f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)\)
50-100 75 9 0.013333 0.119997
100-150 125 10 0.008000 0.080000
150-200 175 17 0.005714 0.097138
200-250 225 10 0.004444 0.044440
250-300 275 5 0.003636 0.018180
300-350 325 4 0.003077 0.012308
350-400 375 5 0.002667 0.013335
Total -- 60 -- 0.385398

Therefore

\[H = \frac{n}{\sum f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)} = \frac{60}{0.385398} \approx 155.68 \text{ liters/minute}\]

The average rate of water flow from irrigation methods is 155.68 liters per minute.

Example 3.9b: Average Speed Covered by Tractors by Indian Farmers

Find the harmonic mean of the speed (km/hr) covered by tractors by farmers in various states of India.

Speed (km/hr) 10-15 15-20 20-25 25-30 30-35 35-40
Number of Tractors (f) 7 12 18 10 8 5

Solution:

We calculate the harmonic mean below:

Speed (km/hr) \(x_i\) f_i \(\frac{1}{x_i}\) \(f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)\)
10-15 12.5 7 0.08000 0.56000
15-20 17.5 12 0.05714 0.68568
20-25 22.5 18 0.04444 0.79992
25-30 27.5 10 0.03636 0.36360
30-35 32.5 8 0.03077 0.24616
35-40 37.5 5 0.02667 0.13335
Total -- 60 -- 2.78871

Therefore

\[H = \frac{n}{\sum f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)} = \frac{60}{2.78871} \approx 21.51 \text{ km/hr}\]

The average speed of tractors is 21.51 km per hour.

Example 3.10a: Geometric and Harmonic Mean of Seed Germination Rate in Haryana

Calculate the geometric and harmonic mean for the following distribution of annual seed germination rates:

\(x_i\) (Germination Rate %) 70 75 80 85 90 95 98
\(f_i\) (Seed Samples) 5 10 15 20 12 8 3

Solution:

We can construct the following table for the calculation of geometric and harmonic means:

\(x_i\) \(f_i\) \(\log x_i\) \(f_i \log x_i\) \(\frac{1}{x_i}\) \(f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)\)
70 5 1.8451 9.2255 0.014286 0.071430
75 10 1.8751 18.7510 0.013333 0.133330
80 15 1.9031 28.5465 0.012500 0.187500
85 20 1.9294 38.5880 0.011765 0.235300
90 12 1.9542 23.4504 0.011111 0.133332
95 8 1.9777 15.8216 0.010526 0.084208
98 3 1.9912 5.9736 0.010204 0.030612
Total 73 -- 140.3566 -- 0.875712

Now

\[\log G = \frac{1}{n} \sum f_i \log x_i = \frac{140.3566}{73} \approx 1.92269\]

Therefore \(G = \text{anti-log}(1.92269) \approx 83.7\) %

And

\[\text{Harmonic mean} = \frac{n}{\sum f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)} = \frac{73}{0.875712} \approx 83.36\]

The geometric mean of seed germination rate is 83.7% and the harmonic mean is 83.36%.

The geometric mean of labor productivity growth rate is 2.857% and the harmonic mean is 2.735%.

2.14 हार्मोनिक mean

हार्मोनिक mean (एचएम) average का एक प्रकार है जो विशेष रूप से दरों, गति या अनुपात वाले data सेट के लिए उपयोगी होता है, खासकर जब अंश (example के लिए, गति में दूरी, दरों में काम की मात्रा) स्थिर होता है।

असमूहीकृत data की परिभाषा:

For a set of \(n\) non-zero values \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_n\), the harmonic mean (denoted as \(H\)) is defined as the reciprocal of the arithmetic mean of the reciprocals of those values:

\[H = \frac{n}{\frac{1}{x_1} + \frac{1}{x_2} + \ldots + \frac{1}{x_n}} = \frac{n}{\sum_{i=1}^{n} \frac{1}{x_i}} \quad (\text{where } x_i \ne 0)\]

application और example:

जब दरों को "x प्रति y" के रूप में व्यक्त किया जाता है और मात्रा "x" स्थिर होती है, तो हार्मोनिक mean उपयोग करने के लिए उपयुक्त average होता है। इसके विपरीत, यदि "y" स्थिर है, तो अंकmathematical mean आमतौर पर अधिक उपयुक्त होता है। एक example पर विचार करें: एक कार पहली 30 किमी 15 किमी/घंटा की गति से, दूसरी 30 किमी 20 किमी/घंटा की गति से और तीसरी 30 किमी 25 किमी/घंटा की गति से चलती है। चूँकि प्रत्येक खंड के लिए दूरी (अंशांक) स्थिर (30 किमी) है, समग्र average गति ज्ञात करने के लिए हार्मोनिक mean सही average है।

इस परिदृश्य में, हार्मोनिक mean की गणना इस प्रकार की जाती है:

\[H = \frac{3}{\frac{1}{15} + \frac{1}{20} + \frac{1}{25}}\]
\[H = \frac{3}{\left(\frac{4+3}{60}\right) + \frac{1}{25}} = \frac{3}{\frac{7}{60} + \frac{1}{25}} = \frac{3}{\frac{35+12}{300}} = \frac{3}{\frac{47}{300}}\]
\[H = \frac{3 \times 300}{47} = \frac{900}{47} \approx 19.15 \text{ km/hr}\]

यह result पूरी यात्रा के दौरान average गति को दर्शाता है।

समूहीकृत frequency distribution की परिभाषा:

For data organized into a grouped frequency distribution with \(k\) classes, having class marks \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_k\) and corresponding frequencies \(f_1, f_2, \ldots, f_k\) (where \(n = \sum_{i=1}^{k} f_i\) is the total number of observations), the harmonic mean is given by:

\[H = \frac{n}{\frac{f_1}{x_1} + \frac{f_2}{x_2} + \ldots + \frac{f_k}{x_k}} = \frac{n}{\sum_{i=1}^{k} \frac{f_i}{x_i}}\]

भारित हार्मोनिक mean:

For a set of values \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_k\) with respective weights \(w_1, w_2, \ldots, w_k\), the weighted harmonic mean (\(H_w\)) is defined as:

\[H_w = \frac{\sum_{i=1}^{k} w_i}{\sum_{i=1}^{k} \frac{w_i}{x_i}}\]

example 3.9ए: हरियाणा में विभिन्न सिंचाई methodयों से जल प्रवाह की average दर

हरियाणा में किसानों द्वारा उपयोग की जाने वाली विभिन्न सिंचाई methodयों से जल प्रवाह की दर (लीटर/मिनट) का हार्मोनिक mean ज्ञात कीजिए।

प्रवाह दर (लीटर/मिनट) 50-100 100-150 150-200 200-250 250-300 300-350 350-400
फ़ील्ड की संख्या (एफ) 9 10 17 10 5 4 5

solution:

हम नीचे हार्मोनिक mean की गणना करते हैं:

प्रवाह दर (लीटर/मिनट) \(x_i\) \(f_i\) \(\frac{1}{x_i}\) \(f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)\)
50-100 75 9 0.013333 0.119997
100-150 125 10 0.008000 0.080000
150-200 175 17 0.005714 0.097138
200-250 225 10 0.004444 0.044440
250-300 275 5 0.003636 0.018180
300-350 325 4 0.003077 0.012308
350-400 375 5 0.002667 0.013335
कुल -- 60 -- 0.385398

इसलिए

\[H = \frac{n}{\sum f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)} = \frac{60}{0.385398} \approx 155.68 \text{ liters/minute}\]

सिंचाई methodयों से जल प्रवाह की average दर 155.68 लीटर प्रति मिनट है।

ट्रैक्टरों की संख्या (च) 7 12 18 10 8 5

ट्रैक्टरों की average गति 21.51 किमी प्रति घंटा है।

example 3.10ए: हरियाणा में बीज अंकुरण दर का ज्यामितीय और हार्मोनिक mean

वार्षिक बीज अंकुरण दर के निम्नलिखित distribution के लिए ज्यामितीय और हार्मोनिक mean की गणना करें:

\(x_i\) (Germination Rate %) 70 75 80 85 90 95 98
\(f_i\) (Seed Samples) 5 10 15 20 12 8 3

solution:

हम ज्यामितीय और हार्मोनिक साधनों की गणना के लिए निम्नलिखित तालिका का निर्माण कर सकते हैं:

\(x_i\) \(f_i\) \(\log x_i\) \(f_i \log x_i\) \(\frac{1}{x_i}\) \(f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)\)
70 5 1.8451 9.2255 0.014286 0.071430
75 10 1.8751 18.7510 0.013333 0.133330
80 15 1.9031 28.5465 0.012500 0.187500
85 20 1.9294 38.5880 0.011765 0.235300
90 12 1.9542 23.4504 0.011111 0.133332
95 8 1.9777 15.8216 0.010526 0.084208
98 3 1.9912 5.9736 0.010204 0.030612
कुल 73 -- 140.3566 -- 0.875712

अब

\[\log G = \frac{1}{n} \sum f_i \log x_i = \frac{140.3566}{73} \approx 1.92269\]

Therefore \(G = \text{anti-log}(1.92269) \approx 83.7\) %

और

\[\text{Harmonic mean} = \frac{n}{\sum f_i \left( \frac{1}{x_i} \right)} = \frac{73}{0.875712} \approx 83.36\]

बीज अंकुरण दर का ज्यामितीय mean 83.7% और हार्मोनिक mean 83.36% है।

2.15 The Median

The Median is a measure of central tendency that represents the middle value in an ordered dataset. It divides the data into two equal halves: 50% of the observations are at or below the median, and 50% are at or above it. Unlike the mean, the median is not affected by extremely large or small values (outliers), making it a robust measure for skewed distributions.

Calculating the Median for Ungrouped Data:

To find the median for a set of \(n\) observations \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_n\):

  1. Order the data: Arrange all observations from the smallest to the largest.
  2. Determine the position:
    • If \(n\) (the total number of observations) is odd, the median is the value at the \((\frac{n+1}{2})^{\text{th}}\) position.
    • If \(n\) is even, the median is the average of the two middle values, specifically the values at the \((\frac{n}{2})^{\text{th}}\) and \((\frac{n}{2}+1)^{\text{th}}\) positions.

For an ungrouped frequency distribution, the median can be identified by constructing a cumulative frequency distribution and locating the value corresponding to the \((\frac{n+1}{2})^{\text{th}}\) or the average of the \((\frac{n}{2})^{\text{th}}\) and \((\frac{n}{2}+1)^{\text{th}}\) observation, similar to ungrouped data, but using cumulative frequencies to find the position.

Calculating the Median for Grouped Frequency Distributions:

For data presented in a grouped frequency distribution, the median represents the value on the horizontal axis that corresponds to a cumulative frequency of \(n/2\). This value lies within a specific class interval, known as the median class or median group.

To obtain a precise median value from grouped data, an assumption is made that the observations are uniformly distributed within the median class. The median is then calculated using the following formula:

\[\text{Median} = L + \left(\frac{\frac{n}{2} - CF}{f}\right) \times h\]

Where:

  • \(L\) = Lower boundary of the median class.
  • \(n\) = Total number of observations (sum of all frequencies).
  • \(CF\) = Cumulative frequency of the class immediately preceding the median class.
  • \(f\) = Frequency of the median class.
  • \(h\) = Class width (or class size) of the median class.

This formula essentially interpolates the median within the median class, assuming a linear distribution of observations within that interval.

2.15 median

मंझला central tendency का एक माप है जो क्रमबद्ध dataसेट में मध्य मान का प्रतिनिधित्व करता है। यह data को दो बराबर हिस्सों में विभाजित करता है: 50% observation median पर या उससे नीचे हैं, और 50% इसके ऊपर या उससे ऊपर हैं। mean के विपरीत, mean अत्यंत बड़े या छोटे values (आउटलेर्स) से प्रभावित नहीं होता है, जिससे यह विषम distributionों के लिए एक मजबूत माप बन जाता है।

अवर्गीकृत data के लिए median की गणना:

To find the median for a set of \(n\) observations \(x_1, x_2, \ldots, x_n\):

  1. data ऑर्डर करें: सभी प्रेक्षणों को छोटे से बड़े तक systematic करें।
  2. स्थिति निर्धारित करें:
    • If \(n\) (the total number of observations) is विषम, the median is the value at the \((\frac{n+1}{2})^{\text{th}}\) position.
    • If \(n\) is यहां तक ​​की, the median is the average of the two middle values, specifically the values at the \((\frac{n}{2})^{\text{th}}\) and \((\frac{n}{2}+1)^{\text{th}}\) positions.

For an ungrouped frequency distribution, the median can be identified by constructing a cumulative frequency distribution and locating the value corresponding to the \((\frac{n+1}{2})^{\text{th}}\) or the average of the \((\frac{n}{2})^{\text{th}}\) and \((\frac{n}{2}+1)^{\text{th}}\) observation, similar to ungrouped data, but using cumulative frequencies to find the position.

समूहीकृत frequency distribution के लिए median की गणना:

For data presented in a grouped frequency distribution, the median represents the value on the horizontal axis that corresponds to a cumulative frequency of \(n/2\). This value lies within a specific class interval, known as the median वर्ग या मध्य समूह.

समूहीकृत data से एक सटीक mean मान प्राप्त करने के लिए, एक धारणा बनाई जाती है कि observation mean वर्ग के भीतर समान रूप से वितरित होते हैं। फिर median की गणना निम्न सूत्र का उपयोग करके की जाती है:

\[\text{Median} = L + \left(\frac{\frac{n}{2} - CF}{f}\right) \times h\]

कहाँ:

  • \(L\) = Lower boundary of the median class.
  • \(n\) = Total number of observations (sum of all frequencies).
  • \(CF\) = Cumulative frequency of the class immediately preceding the median class.
  • \(f\) = Frequency of the median class.
  • \(h\) = Class width (or class size) of the median class.

यह सूत्र अनिवार्य रूप से उस अंतराल के भीतर observationों के रैखिक distribution को मानते हुए, median वर्ग के भीतर median को प्रक्षेपित करता है।

2.15.1 Quantiles

In statistics, when dealing with large datasets, it is often useful to divide the data into several equal parts to understand its distribution more comprehensively. These division points are collectively known as Quantiles or Fractiles.

Types of Quantiles:

  • Quartiles:

    These are three specific values that divide an ordered dataset into four equal parts. They are denoted as \(Q_1\), \(Q_2\), and \(Q_3\):

    • \(Q_1\) (First or Lower Quartile): The value below which 25% of the data falls.
    • \(Q_2\) (Second Quartile): The value below which 50% of the data falls. This is equivalent to the median.
    • \(Q_3\) (Third or Upper Quartile): The value below which 75% of the data falls.

  • Deciles:

    These are nine values that divide an ordered dataset into ten equal parts. They are denoted as \(D_1, D_2, \ldots, D_9\). For instance, \(D_1\) is the value below which 10% of the data falls, and \(D_5\) is equivalent to the median.

  • Percentiles:

    These are 99 values that divide an ordered dataset into one hundred equal parts. They are denoted as \(P_1, P_2, \ldots, P_{99}\). \(P_j\) is the value below which \(j\) percent of the data falls. For example, \(P_{25}\) is equivalent to \(Q_1\), \(P_{50}\) is the median (\(Q_2\) or \(D_5\)), and \(P_{75}\) is equivalent to \(Q_3\).

Calculating Quantiles for Ungrouped Data:

For a set of \(n\) observations arranged in ascending order, the \(j\)-th percentile, \(P_j\), can be calculated using the following rules:

  1. If \(jn/100\) is not an integer, the \(j\)-th percentile is the observation located at the position given by:

    \[\text{Position} = \lfloor \frac{jn}{100} \rfloor + 1\]
    where \(\lfloor x \rfloor\) denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to \(x\).

  2. If \(jn/100\) **is an integer**, the \(j\)-th percentile is the average of the observations at the following two positions:

    \[\text{Position 1} = \frac{jn}{100}\]
    \[\text{Position 2} = \frac{jn}{100} + 1\]

Calculating Quantiles for Grouped Data:

For data presented in a grouped frequency distribution, the calculation of quantiles (quartiles, deciles, percentiles) follows a method similar to that used for the median. The general formula for the \(j\)-th percentile \(P_j\) for grouped data is:

\[P_j = L + \left(\frac{\frac{jn}{100} - CF}{f}\right) \times h\]

Where:

  • \(L\) = Lower boundary of the class containing the \(j\)-th percentile.
  • \(n\) = Total number of observations (sum of all frequencies).
  • \(CF\) = Cumulative frequency of the class immediately preceding the percentile class.
  • \(f\) = Frequency of the percentile class.
  • \(h\) = Class width of the percentile class.

Historical Note:

The terms "median" and "percentile" are often attributed to Sir Francis Galton (1822–1911), although the concept of the median was earlier suggested by Carl Friedrich Gauss (1777–1855).

Example 3.11a: Daily Milk Production (liters) per Cow in a Village in Haryana

The daily milk production (in liters) per cow of 9 cows in a village in Haryana is as follows:

8, 6, 7, 9, 7.5, 6.5, 8.5, 9.2, 7

Find the median and quartiles.

Solution:

To find the median and quartiles, we first arrange the milk production from lowest to highest.

The ordered milk production values are:

6, 6.5, 7, 7, 7.5, 8, 8.5, 9, 9.2

Here \(n=9\) and \(n/2 = 9/2 = 4.5\), i.e., \(n/2\) is not an integer, so

Median = Quantity of milk produced by the \(\left[ \frac{n}{2} \right] + 1\)th cow

= (4+1), i.e., the quantity of milk produced by the 5th cow in the ordered data

= 7.5 liters

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 9/4 = 2.25\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_1 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 9/4 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 3rd observation

= 7 liters

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 9)/4 = 27/4 = 6.75\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_3 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{3n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 6.75 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 7th observation

= 8.5 liters

Example 3.11b: Quality Score of Crop Seeds in Various Regions of India

The quality scores (0-100) of crop seeds collected from 10 different regions of India are as follows:

72, 85, 68, 91, 78, 80, 75, 88, 70, 82

Find the median and quartiles.

Solution:

To find the median and quartiles, we first arrange the quality scores from lowest to highest.

The ordered scores are:

68, 70, 72, 75, 78, 80, 82, 85, 88, 91

Here \(n=10\) and \(n/2 = 10/2 = 5\), i.e., \(n/2\) is an integer, so

Median = Average of the \((\frac{n}{2})^{th}\) and \((\frac{n}{2}+1)^{th}\) observations

= Average of the 5th and 6th observation = \(\frac{78 + 80}{2} = 79\)

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 10/4 = 2.5\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_1 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 2.5 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 3rd observation

= 72

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 10)/4 = 30/4 = 7.5\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_3 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{3n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 7.5 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 8th observation

= 85

Example 3.12a: Median and Quartiles from the Frequency Distribution of Average Livestock Weight in Haryana

Find the median, first and third quartiles from the given frequency distribution of average livestock weight (in kilograms).

Weight (kg) 50-100 100-150 150-200 200-250 250-300 300-350 350-400
Number of Animals (f) 8 12 15 10 7 5 3

Solution:

To find the median and quartiles, we construct the following cumulative frequency table:

Weight (kg) f Cumulative Frequency
50-100 8 8
100-150 12 20
150-200 15 35
200-250 10 45
250-300 7 52
300-350 5 57
350-400 3 60

The total frequency \(n = 60\), so \(n/2 = 30\), which indicates that 30 observations are at or below the median. From the cumulative frequency table, we find that the 30th observation falls in the class 150-200 (median class), and we have:

\(l = 150\), \(h = 50\), \(C = 20\), \(f = 15\)

Therefore

\[\text{Median} = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{2} - C}{f} \right) = 150 + 50 \left( \frac{30 - 20}{15} \right) = 150 + 50 \left( \frac{10}{15} \right) = 150 + 50(0.6667) = 150 + 33.33 = 183.33 \text{ kilograms}\]

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 60/4 = 15\)

From the cumulative frequency table, we see that the 15th observation falls in the class 100-150.

Therefore \(l = 100\), \(h = 50\), \(C = 8\), \(f = 12\)

\[Q_1 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 100 + 50 \left( \frac{15 - 8}{12} \right) = 100 + 50 \left( \frac{7}{12} \right) = 100 + 50(0.5833) = 100 + 29.16 = 129.16 \text{ kilograms}\]

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 60)/4 = 45\)

From the cumulative frequency table, the 45th observation falls in the class 200-250.

Therefore \(l = 200\), \(h = 50\), \(C = 35\), \(f = 10\)

\[Q_3 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{3n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 200 + 50 \left( \frac{45 - 35}{10} \right) = 200 + 50 \left( \frac{10}{10} \right) = 200 + 50(1) = 250 \text{ kilograms}\]

Example 3.12b: Median and Quartiles of Land Holding Size of Farmers in India

Find the median, first and third quartiles from the frequency distribution of land holding size (in acres) of farmers in India.

Holding Size (acres) 0-2 2-5 5-10 10-20 20-50 50-100
Number of Farmers (f) 100 150 80 50 15 5

Solution:

To find the median and quartiles, we construct the following cumulative frequency table:

Holding Size (acres) f Cumulative Frequency
0-2 100 100
2-5 150 250
5-10 80 330
10-20 50 380
20-50 15 395
50-100 5 400

The total frequency \(n = 400\), so \(n/2 = 200\), which indicates that 200 observations are at or below the median. From the cumulative frequency table, we find that the 200th observation falls in the class 2-5 (median class), and we have:

\(l = 2\), \(h = 3\), \(C = 100\), \(f = 150\)

Therefore

\[\text{Median} = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{2} - C}{f} \right) = 2 + 3 \left( \frac{200 - 100}{150} \right) = 2 + 3 \left( \frac{100}{150} \right) = 2 + 3(0.6667) = 2 + 2 = 4 \text{ acres}\]

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 400/4 = 100\)

From the cumulative frequency table, we see that the 100th observation falls in the class 0-2.

Therefore \(l = 0\), \(h = 2\), \(C = 0\), \(f = 100\)

\[Q_1 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 0 + 2 \left( \frac{100 - 0}{100} \right) = 0 + 2 \left( \frac{100}{100} \right) = 0 + 2(1) = 2 \text{ acres}\]

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 400)/4 = 300\)

From the cumulative frequency table, the 300th observation falls in the class 5-10.

Therefore \(l = 5\), \(h = 5\), \(C = 250\), \(f = 80\)

\[Q_3 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{3n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 5 + 5 \left( \frac{300 - 250}{80} \right) = 5 + 5 \left( \frac{50}{80} \right) = 5 + 5(0.625) = 5 + 3.125 = 8.125 \text{ acres}\]

2.15.1 मात्राएँ

data में, बड़े dataसेट के साथ काम करते समय, इसके distribution को अधिक व्यापक रूप से समझने के लिए data को कई समान भागों में विभाजित करना अक्सर उपयोगी होता है। इन विभाजन बिंदुओं को सामूहिक रूप से जाना जाता है मात्राएँ या भग्न.

मात्राओं के प्रकार:

  • चतुर्थक:

    These are three specific values that divide an ordered dataset into four equal parts. They are denoted as \(Q_1\), \(Q_2\), and \(Q_3\):

    • \(Q_1\) (First or Lower Quartile): The value below which 25% of the data falls.
    • \(Q_2\) (Second Quartile): The value below which 50% of the data falls. This is equivalent to the median.
    • \(Q_3\) (Third or Upper Quartile): The value below which 75% of the data falls.

  • दशमांश:

    These are nine values that divide an ordered dataset into ten equal parts. They are denoted as \(D_1, D_2, \ldots, D_9\). For instance, \(D_1\) is the value below which 10% of the data falls, and \(D_5\) is equivalent to the median.

  • प्रतिशतक:

    These are 99 values that divide an ordered dataset into one hundred equal parts. They are denoted as \(P_1, P_2, \ldots, P_{99}\). \(P_j\) is the value below which \(j\) percent of the data falls. For example, \(P_{25}\) is equivalent to \(Q_1\), \(P_{50}\) is the median (\(Q_2\) or \(D_5\)), and \(P_{75}\) is equivalent to \(Q_3\).

अवर्गीकृत data के लिए मात्राओं की गणना:

For a set of \(n\) observations arranged in ascending order, the \(j\)-th percentile, \(P_j\), can be calculated using the following rules:

  1. If \(jn/100\) is पूर्णांक नहीं, the \(j\)-th percentile is the observation located at the position given by:

    \[\text{Position} = \lfloor \frac{jn}{100} \rfloor + 1\]
    where \(\lfloor x \rfloor\) denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to \(x\).

  2. If \(jn/100\) **is an integer**, the \(j\)-th percentile is the average of the observations at the following two positions:

    \[\text{Position 1} = \frac{jn}{100}\]
    \[\text{Position 2} = \frac{jn}{100} + 1\]

समूहीकृत data के लिए मात्राओं की गणना:

For data presented in a grouped frequency distribution, the calculation of quantiles (quartiles, deciles, percentiles) follows a method similar to that used for the median. The general formula for the \(j\)-th percentile \(P_j\) for grouped data is:

\[P_j = L + \left(\frac{\frac{jn}{100} - CF}{f}\right) \times h\]

कहाँ:

  • \(L\) = Lower boundary of the class containing the \(j\)-th percentile.
  • \(n\) = Total number of observations (sum of all frequencies).
  • \(CF\) = Cumulative frequency of the class immediately preceding the percentile class.
  • \(f\) = Frequency of the percentile class.
  • \(h\) = Class width of the percentile class.

ऐतिहासिक नोट:

शब्द "median" और "प्रतिशतक" का श्रेय अक्सर सर फ्रांसिस गैल्टन (1822-1911) को दिया जाता है, हालांकि median की अवधारणा पहले कार्ल फ्रेडरिक गॉस (1777-1855) द्वारा सुझाई गई थी।

example 3.11ए: हरियाणा के एक गांव में प्रति गाय दैनिक दूध उत्पादन (लीटर)।

हरियाणा के एक गाँव में 9 गायों का प्रति गाय दैनिक दूध उत्पादन (लीटर में) इस प्रकार है:

8, 6, 7, 9, 7.5, 6.5, 8.5, 9.2, 7

median और चतुर्थक ज्ञात कीजिए।

solution:

median और चतुर्थक ज्ञात करने के लिए, हम पहले दूध उत्पादन को न्यूनतम से उच्चतम की ओर systematic करते हैं।

आदेशित दूध उत्पादन value हैं:

6, 6.5, 7, 7, 7.5, 8, 8.5, 9, 9.2

Here \(n=9\) and \(n/2 = 9/2 = 4.5\), i.e., \(n/2\) is not an integer, so

Median = Quantity of milk produced by the \(\left[ \frac{n}{2} \right] + 1\)th cow

= (4+1), यानी, ऑर्डर किए गए data में 5वीं गाय द्वारा उत्पादित दूध की मात्रा

= 7.5 लीटर

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 9/4 = 2.25\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_1 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 9/4 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 3rd observation

= 7 लीटर

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 9)/4 = 27/4 = 6.75\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_3 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{3n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 6.75 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 7th observation

= 8.5 लीटर

example 3.11बी: भारत के विभिन्न fieldों में फसल बीजों का attributeवत्ता स्कोर

भारत के 10 विभिन्न fieldों से एकत्रित फसल बीजों के attributeवत्ता स्कोर (0-100) इस प्रकार हैं:

72, 85, 68, 91, 78, 80, 75, 88, 70, 82

median और चतुर्थक ज्ञात कीजिए।

solution:

median और चतुर्थक ज्ञात करने के लिए, हम पहले attributeवत्ता स्कोर को निम्नतम से उच्चतम तक systematic करते हैं।

क्रमबद्ध स्कोर हैं:

68, 70, 72, 75, 78, 80, 82, 85, 88, 91

Here \(n=10\) and \(n/2 = 10/2 = 5\), i.e., \(n/2\) is an integer, so

Median = Average of the \((\frac{n}{2})^{th}\) and \((\frac{n}{2}+1)^{th}\) observations

= Average of the 5th and 6th observation = \(\frac{78 + 80}{2} = 79\)

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 10/4 = 2.5\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_1 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 2.5 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 3rd observation

= 72

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 10)/4 = 30/4 = 7.5\), which is not an integer.

\[Q_3 = \text{ Observation with ordinal number } \left[ \frac{3n}{4} \right] + 1\]

= \(\left[ 7.5 \right] + 1\)th, i.e., the 8th observation

= 85

example 3.12ए: हरियाणा में average पशुधन वजन के frequency distribution से median और चतुर्थक

average पशुधन वजन (किलोग्राम में) के दिए गए frequency distribution से median , प्रथम और तृतीय चतुर्थक ज्ञात कीजिए।

वजन (किलो) 50-100 100-150 150-200 200-250 250-300 300-350 350-400
पशुओं की संख्या (च) 8 12 15 10 7 5 3

solution:

median और चतुर्थक ज्ञात करने के लिए, हम निम्नलिखित संचयी frequency तालिका बनाते हैं:

वजन (किलो) एफ संचयी frequency
50-100 8 8
100-150 12 20
150-200 15 35
200-250 10 45
250-300 7 52
300-350 5 57
350-400 3 60

The total frequency \(n = 60\), so \(n/2 = 30\), which indicates that 30 observations are at or below the median. From the cumulative frequency table, we find that the 30th observation falls in the class 150-200 (median class), and we have:

\(l = 150\), \(h = 50\), \(C = 20\), \(f = 15\)

इसलिए

\[\text{Median} = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{2} - C}{f} \right) = 150 + 50 \left( \frac{30 - 20}{15} \right) = 150 + 50 \left( \frac{10}{15} \right) = 150 + 50(0.6667) = 150 + 33.33 = 183.33 \text{ kilograms}\]

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 60/4 = 15\)

संचयी frequency तालिका से, हम देखते हैं कि 15वाँ observation 100-150 वर्ग में आता है।

Therefore \(l = 100\), \(h = 50\), \(C = 8\), \(f = 12\)

\[Q_1 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 100 + 50 \left( \frac{15 - 8}{12} \right) = 100 + 50 \left( \frac{7}{12} \right) = 100 + 50(0.5833) = 100 + 29.16 = 129.16 \text{ kilograms}\]

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 60)/4 = 45\)

संचयी frequency तालिका से, 45वां observation 200-250 वर्ग में आता है।

Therefore \(l = 200\), \(h = 50\), \(C = 35\), \(f = 10\)

\[Q_3 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{3n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 200 + 50 \left( \frac{45 - 35}{10} \right) = 200 + 50 \left( \frac{10}{10} \right) = 200 + 50(1) = 250 \text{ kilograms}\]

example 3.12बी: भारत में किसानों की भूमि जोत के size का median और चतुर्थांश

भारत में किसानों की भूमि जोत के size (एकड़ में) के बारंबारता distribution से mean , प्रथम और तृतीय चतुर्थक ज्ञात कीजिए।

जोत का size (एकड़) 0-2 2-5 5-10 10-20 20-50 50-100
किसानों की संख्या (एफ) 100 150 80 50 15 5

solution:

median और चतुर्थक ज्ञात करने के लिए, हम निम्नलिखित संचयी frequency तालिका बनाते हैं:

जोत का size (एकड़) एफ संचयी frequency
0-2 100 100
2-5 150 250
5-10 80 330
10-20 50 380
20-50 15 395
50-100 5 400

The total frequency \(n = 400\), so \(n/2 = 200\), which indicates that 200 observations are at or below the median. From the cumulative frequency table, we find that the 200th observation falls in the class 2-5 (median class), and we have:

\(l = 2\), \(h = 3\), \(C = 100\), \(f = 150\)

इसलिए

\[\text{Median} = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{2} - C}{f} \right) = 2 + 3 \left( \frac{200 - 100}{150} \right) = 2 + 3 \left( \frac{100}{150} \right) = 2 + 3(0.6667) = 2 + 2 = 4 \text{ acres}\]

For \(Q_1\), we have \(n/4 = 400/4 = 100\)

संचयी frequency तालिका से, हम देखते हैं कि 100वाँ observation वर्ग 0-2 में आता है।

Therefore \(l = 0\), \(h = 2\), \(C = 0\), \(f = 100\)

\[Q_1 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 0 + 2 \left( \frac{100 - 0}{100} \right) = 0 + 2 \left( \frac{100}{100} \right) = 0 + 2(1) = 2 \text{ acres}\]

For \(Q_3\), we have \(3n/4 = (3 \times 400)/4 = 300\)

संचयी frequency तालिका से, 300वां observation कक्षा 5-10 में आता है।

Therefore \(l = 5\), \(h = 5\), \(C = 250\), \(f = 80\)

\[Q_3 = l + h \left( \frac{\frac{3n}{4} - C}{f} \right) = 5 + 5 \left( \frac{300 - 250}{80} \right) = 5 + 5 \left( \frac{50}{80} \right) = 5 + 5(0.625) = 5 + 3.125 = 8.125 \text{ acres}\]

2.16 The Mode

The Mode is a measure of central tendency that represents the value or values that occur most frequently in a dataset or distribution. It signifies the most typical observation within the data.

Characteristics of the Mode:

  • Unimodal: A distribution with only one mode.
  • Bimodal: A distribution with two modes, indicating two distinct peaks in frequency.
  • Multimodal: A distribution with more than two modes.
  • Unlike the mean and median, the mode can be used with categorical data (non-numeric data).

Calculating the Mode for Ungrouped Data:

For ungrouped data or an ungrouped frequency distribution, the mode is directly identified as the value of the variable that has the highest frequency of occurrence.

Calculating the Mode for Grouped Frequency Distributions:

For data presented in a grouped frequency distribution with equal class intervals, a specific value for the mode is typically estimated. First, the **modal class** is identified as the class interval with the highest frequency. The mode is then calculated using the following formula, which interpolates within the modal class:

\[\text{Mode} = L + \left( \frac{d_1}{d_1 + d_2} \right) \times h\]

Where:

  • \(L\) = Lower boundary of the modal class.
  • \(h\) = Width of the class interval of the modal class.
  • \(d_1\) = The difference between the frequency of the modal class and the frequency of the class immediately preceding it.
  • \(d_2\) = The difference between the frequency of the modal class and the frequency of the class immediately succeeding it.

This formula provides an estimate of the mode, assuming a specific distribution pattern of frequencies around the modal class.

Example 3.13a: Mode of Daily Temperature in an Agricultural Farm in Haryana

Find the mode of the frequency distribution for daily temperature (in degrees Celsius) in an agricultural farm:

Temperature (°C) 20-25 25-30 30-35 35-40 40-45 45-50
Number of Days (f) 8 12 25 18 10 5

Solution:

The highest frequency is 25, which falls in the class 30-35. Therefore, the modal class is 30-35, and we have:

\(l = 30\), \(h = 5\), \(d_1 = 25 - 12 = 13\), \(d_2 = 25 - 18 = 7\)

\[\text{Mode} = l + h \left( \frac{d_1}{d_1 + d_2} \right) = 30 + 5 \left( \frac{13}{13 + 7} \right) = 30 + 5 \left( \frac{13}{20} \right) = 30 + 5(0.65) = 30 + 3.25 = 33.25 \text{ °C}\]

Example 3.13b: Mode of the Number of Cattle per Household among Indian Farmers

Find the mode of the frequency distribution for the number of cattle per household among Indian farmers:

Number of Cattle 0-5 5-10 10-15 15-20 20-25 25-30
Number of Households (f) 150 200 280 120 50 20

Solution:

The highest frequency is 280, which falls in the class 10-15. Therefore, the modal class is 10-15, and we have:

\(l = 10\), \(h = 5\), \(d_1 = 280 - 200 = 80\), \(d_2 = 280 - 120 = 160\)

\[\text{Mode} = l + h \left( \frac{d_1}{d_1 + d_2} \right) = 10 + 5 \left( \frac{80}{80 + 160} \right) = 10 + 5 \left( \frac{80}{240} \right) = 10 + 5(0.3333) = 10 + 1.6665 = 11.67 \text{ cattle}\]

2.16 मोड

तरीका central tendency का एक माप है जो किसी dataसेट या distribution में सबसे अधिक बार होने वाले value या values का प्रतिनिधित्व करता है। यह data के भीतर सबसे विशिष्ट observation का प्रतीक है।

मोड के लक्षण:

  • यूनिmodel: केवल एक मोड वाला distribution .
  • बिmodel: दो मोड वाला एक distribution , जो frequency में दो अलग-अलग शिखरों को दर्शाता है।
  • मल्टीmodel: दो से अधिक मोड वाला distribution .
  • mean और median के विपरीत, मोड का उपयोग श्रेणीबद्ध data (गैर-संख्यात्मक data) के साथ किया जा सकता है।

असमूहीकृत data के लिए मोड की गणना:

असमूहीकृत data या असमूहीकृत frequency distribution के लिए, मोड को सीधे उस variable के मान के रूप में पहचाना जाता है जिसमें घटना की frequency सबसे अधिक होती है।

समूहीकृत frequency distribution के लिए मोड की गणना:

समान वर्ग अंतराल के साथ समूहीकृत frequency distribution में प्रस्तुत data के लिए, मोड के लिए एक विशिष्ट मान आमतौर पर estimationित किया जाता है। सबसे पहले, **मोडल क्लास** को उच्चतम frequency वाले वर्ग अंतराल के रूप में पहचाना जाता है। फिर मोड की गणना निम्न सूत्र का उपयोग करके की जाती है, जो मोडल वर्ग के भीतर प्रक्षेपित होता है:

\[\text{Mode} = L + \left( \frac{d_1}{d_1 + d_2} \right) \times h\]

कहाँ:

  • \(L\) = Lower boundary of the modal class.
  • \(h\) = Width of the class interval of the modal class.
  • \(d_1\) = The difference between the frequency of the modal class and the frequency of the class immediately preceding it.
  • \(d_2\) = The difference between the frequency of the modal class and the frequency of the class immediately succeeding it.

यह सूत्र मोडल वर्ग के आसपास frequencyयों के एक विशिष्ट distribution पैटर्न को मानते हुए, मोड का estimation provide करता है।

example 3.13ए: हरियाणा में एक कृषि फार्म में दैनिक तापमान का तरीका

एक कृषि फार्म में दैनिक तापमान (डिग्री सेल्सियस में) के लिए frequency distribution का तरीका खोजें:

तापमान (डिग्री सेल्सियस) 20-25 25-30 30-35 35-40 40-45 45-50
दिनों की संख्या (एफ) 8 12 25 18 10 5

solution:

उच्चतम frequency 25 है, जो 30-35 वर्ग में आती है। इसलिए, मोडल क्लास 30-35 है, और हमारे पास है:

\(l = 30\), \(h = 5\), \(d_1 = 25 - 12 = 13\), \(d_2 = 25 - 18 = 7\)

\[\text{Mode} = l + h \left( \frac{d_1}{d_1 + d_2} \right) = 30 + 5 \left( \frac{13}{13 + 7} \right) = 30 + 5 \left( \frac{13}{20} \right) = 30 + 5(0.65) = 30 + 3.25 = 33.25 \text{ °C}\]

example 3.13बी: भारतीय किसानों के बीच प्रति परिवार मवेशियों की संख्या का तरीका

भारतीय किसानों के बीच प्रति परिवार मवेशियों की संख्या के लिए frequency distribution का तरीका खोजें:

मवेशियों की संख्या 0-5 5-10 10-15 15-20 20-25 25-30
परिवारों की संख्या (च) 150 200 280 120 50 20

solution:

उच्चतम frequency 280 है, जो कक्षा 10-15 में आती है। इसलिए, मोडल क्लास 10-15 है, और हमारे पास है:

\(l = 10\), \(h = 5\), \(d_1 = 280 - 200 = 80\), \(d_2 = 280 - 120 = 160\)

\[\text{Mode} = l + h \left( \frac{d_1}{d_1 + d_2} \right) = 10 + 5 \left( \frac{80}{80 + 160} \right) = 10 + 5 \left( \frac{80}{240} \right) = 10 + 5(0.3333) = 10 + 1.6665 = 11.67 \text{ cattle}\]

2.17 Emprical Relationship Between Mean, Median and Mode

For moderately asymmetrical distributions, the empirical relationship between mean, median and mode is as follows:

\[\text{Mode} \approx 3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean})\]
or
\[\text{Mean} - \text{Mode} \approx 3(\text{Mean} - \text{Median})\]

This relationship is approximately true for a normal curve and any symmetrical distribution.

Example 3.14a: Empirical Relationship for Wheat Yield in an Agricultural Farm

For the distribution of wheat yield given in the previous example, we had:

  • Mean = 50.6 quintals
  • Median = 50.8 quintals (approximate)
  • Mode = 48.5 quintals (approximate)

Verify the empirical relationship.

Solution:

Now \(3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean}) = 3(50.8) - 2(50.6) = 152.4 - 101.2 = 51.2\) quintals, which is reasonably close to the calculated mode of 48.5 quintals.

Example 3.14b: Empirical Relationship for Annual Income of Indian Farmers

For the annual income (in lakh rupees) of Indian farmers, suppose we have:

  • Mean = 3.1 lakh rupees
  • Median = 3.05 lakh rupees
  • Mode = 2.9 lakh rupees

Verify the empirical relationship.

Solution:

Now \(3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean}) = 3(3.05) - 2(3.1) = 9.15 - 6.2 = 2.95\) lakh rupees, which is reasonably close to the calculated mode of 2.9 lakh rupees.

2.17 mean , median और mode के बीच अनुभवजन्य association

मध्यम असममित distribution के लिए, mean , median और mode के बीच अनुभवजन्य association इस प्रकार है:

\[\text{Mode} \approx 3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean})\]
या
\[\text{Mean} - \text{Mode} \approx 3(\text{Mean} - \text{Median})\]

यह association सामान्य वक्र और किसी भी सममित distribution के लिए लगभग सत्य है।

example 3.14ए: कृषि फार्म में गेहूं की yield के लिए अनुभवजन्य association

पिछले example में दिए गए गेहूं की yield के distribution के लिए, हमारे पास था:

  • mean = 50.6 क्विंटल
  • mean = 50.8 क्विंटल (estimationित)
  • मोड = 48.5 क्विंटल (estimationित)

अनुभवजन्य association सत्यापित करें.

solution:

Now \(3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean}) = 3(50.8) - 2(50.6) = 152.4 - 101.2 = 51.2\) quintals, which is reasonably close to the calculated mode of 48.5 quintals.

example 3.14बी: भारतीय किसानों की वार्षिक आय के लिए अनुभवजन्य association

भारतीय किसानों की वार्षिक आय (लाख रुपये में) के लिए, मान लीजिए:

  • mean = 3.1 लाख रुपये
  • mean = 3.05 लाख रुपये
  • मोड = 2.9 लाख रुपये

अनुभवजन्य association सत्यापित करें.

solution:

Now \(3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean}) = 3(3.05) - 2(3.1) = 9.15 - 6.2 = 2.95\) lakh rupees, which is reasonably close to the calculated mode of 2.9 lakh rupees.

2.18 Relative Merits and Demarits of Measures of Central Tandencies

Each of the averages we have discussed has its own merits and demerits, and is useful in certain situations. We list below the merits and demerits of the different averages.

3.10.1 The Arithmetic Mean

Merits:

  1. It is easy to understand and simple to calculate.
  2. It is based on all observations.
  3. It is capable of further algebraic treatment.
  4. It is a stable average as it is least affected by fluctuations of sampling.
  5. The sum of deviations from the arithmetic mean is always zero.
  6. The sum of squares of deviations from the mean is minimum.

Demerits:

  1. It is unduly influenced by extreme values.
  2. It cannot be calculated for distributions with open-end classes.
  3. It may not be a value actually observed in the data.
  4. It cannot be determined by inspection or graphical method.

3.10.2 The Geometric Mean

Merits:

  1. It is based on all observations.
  2. It is not unduly influenced by extreme values.
  3. It gives proper results when averaging ratios, percentages, and rates of change.
  4. It is capable of algebraic treatment.

Demerits:

  1. It is relatively difficult to understand.
  2. It cannot be easily calculated.
  3. It cannot be calculated if the value of any observation is negative or zero.
  4. It is always less than the arithmetic mean except when all observations are equal.
  5. It gives too much importance to smaller items.

3.10.3 The Harmonic Mean

Merits:

  1. It is based on all observations.
  2. It can be used to average ratios or rates, especially when the numerator is kept constant.
  3. It gives minimum importance to larger items.

Demerits:

  1. It is difficult to understand and calculate.
  2. It cannot be calculated if the value of any observation is zero or negative.
  3. It gives too much importance to smaller items.
  4. It is always less than the arithmetic mean and geometric mean except when all observations are equal.

3.10.4 The Median

Merits:

  1. It is easy to understand and calculate.
  2. It can be located graphically.
  3. It can be calculated for distributions with open-end classes.
  4. It is not unduly influenced by extreme values.
  5. It can also be determined when some information about the data is unavailable.

Demerits:

  1. It is not based on all observations.
  2. It is not capable of further mathematical treatment.
  3. It is not a stable average as it is affected by fluctuations of sampling.

3.10.5 The Mode

Merits:

  1. It is easy to understand.
  2. It can be located graphically.
  3. It can be determined for qualitative data.
  4. It is not affected by extreme values.
  5. It is the most typical value.

Demerits:

  1. It is not based on all observations.
  2. It is not capable of further mathematical treatment.
  3. In some cases, it is ill-defined.
  4. It is the least stable among all averages.

2.18 central tendencyयों के मापों के सापेक्ष attribute और दोष

हमने जिन averageों पर variable्चा की है उनमें से प्रत्येक के अपने attribute और दोष हैं, और कुछ स्थितियों में उपयोगी है। हम विभिन्न averageों के attribute और दोषों को नीचे सूचीबद्ध करते हैं।

3.10.1 अंकmathematical mean

attribute:

  1. इसे समझना आसान है और गणना करना भी आसान है।
  2. यह सभी observationों पर आधारित है।
  3. यह आगे बीजmathematical उपचार करने में सक्षम है।
  4. यह एक स्थिर average है क्योंकि यह samples के उतार-चढ़ाव से सबसे कम प्रभावित होता है।
  5. अंकmathematical mean से विचलन का योग सदैव शून्य होता है।
  6. mean से विचलन के वर्गों का योग न्यूनतम होता है।

अवattribute:

  1. यह अत्यधिक values से अनावश्यक रूप से प्रभावित है।
  2. इसकी गणना ओपन-एंड कक्षाओं वाले distributionों के लिए नहीं की जा सकती।
  3. यह वास्तव में data में देखा गया मान नहीं हो सकता है।
  4. इसे निरीक्षण या graph़िकल method द्वारा निर्धारित नहीं किया जा सकता है।

3.10.2 ज्यामितीय mean

attribute:

  1. यह सभी observationों पर आधारित है।
  2. यह variableम values से अनावश्यक रूप से प्रभावित नहीं है।
  3. अनुपात, प्रतिशत और परिवर्तन की दर का average निकालने पर यह उचित result देता है।
  4. यह बीजmathematical उपचार करने में सक्षम है।

अवattribute:

  1. इसे समझना अपेक्षाकृत कठिन है।
  2. इसकी गणना आसानी से नहीं की जा सकती.
  3. यदि किसी observation का मान ऋणात्मक या शून्य है तो इसकी गणना नहीं की जा सकती।
  4. यह हमेशा अंकmathematical mean से कम होता है, सिवाय इसके कि जब सभी observation समान हों।
  5. यह छोटी वस्तुओं को बहुत अधिक महत्व देता है।

3.10.3 हार्मोनिक mean

attribute:

  1. यह सभी observationों पर आधारित है।
  2. इसका उपयोग अनुपातों या दरों को average करने के लिए किया जा सकता है, खासकर जब अंश को स्थिर रखा जाता है।
  3. यह बड़ी वस्तुओं को न्यूनतम महत्व देता है।

अवattribute:

  1. इसे समझना और गणना करना कठिन है।
  2. यदि किसी observation का मान शून्य या ऋणात्मक है तो इसकी गणना नहीं की जा सकती।
  3. यह छोटी वस्तुओं को बहुत अधिक महत्व देता है।
  4. यह हमेशा अंकmathematical mean और ज्यामितीय mean से कम होता है, सिवाय इसके कि जब सभी observation समान हों।

3.10.4 median

attribute:

  1. इसे समझना और गणना करना आसान है।
  2. इसे graph़िक रूप से स्थित किया जा सकता है.
  3. इसकी गणना ओपन-एंड कक्षाओं वाले distribution के लिए की जा सकती है।
  4. यह variableम values से अनावश्यक रूप से प्रभावित नहीं है।
  5. यह तब भी निर्धारित किया जा सकता है जब data के बारे में कुछ information अनुपलब्ध हो।

अवattribute:

  1. यह सभी observationों पर आधारित नहीं है।
  2. यह आगे mathematical उपचार करने में सक्षम नहीं है।
  3. यह एक स्थिर average नहीं है क्योंकि यह samples के उतार-चढ़ाव से प्रभावित होता है।

3.10.5 मोड

attribute:

  1. इसे समझना आसान है.
  2. इसे graph़िक रूप से स्थित किया जा सकता है.
  3. इसे qualitative data के लिए निर्धारित किया जा सकता है।
  4. यह अतिवादी values से प्रभावित नहीं होता।
  5. यह सबसे विशिष्ट value है.

अवattribute:

  1. यह सभी observationों पर आधारित नहीं है।
  2. यह आगे mathematical उपचार करने में सक्षम नहीं है।
  3. कुछ मामलों में, यह अपरिभाषित है।
  4. यह सभी averageों में सबसे कम स्थिर है।

2.19 When to Choose which Measure of Central Tendacies

Each measure of central tendency possesses distinct strengths and limitations; consequently, the choice of an appropriate average depends on the characteristics of the data and the analytical objective. The following guidelines assist in selecting a suitable average:

  • Symmetrical distributions: When the frequency distribution is roughly symmetric, the mean, median, and mode are nearly equal. In such cases, the arithmetic mean is preferred because of its desirable mathematical properties (e.g., linearity, algebraic manipulability).
  • Skewed distributions: For markedly skewed data, the median (robust to outliers) or the mode (indicates the most frequent value) provides a more representative summary than the mean.
  • Open‑ended class intervals: When the data contain open‑ended (unbounded) classes, the median is generally favored because it does not require knowledge of the extreme values.
  • Only totals are available: If the only information supplied is the aggregate total and the number of observations, the arithmetic mean is the sole feasible average.
  • Averaging ratios or rates of change: The geometric mean is theoretically optimal for multiplicative quantities such as growth rates, index numbers, or ratios. When the numerator is held constant (e.g., speeds, travel times), the harmonic mean is more appropriate.
  • Empirical relationship for skewed data: When the mean is unsuitable and the other averages are difficult to compute, the empirical approximation Mean–Mode≈3(Mean–Median) may be employed as a rough adjustment.
  • Pricing of heterogeneous items: For aggregating prices of disparate goods (e.g., furniture, appliances), the mode often reflects the most common price level and can be more informative than the mean.
  • Equal‑period rates of change: When rates are measured over equal time intervals (e.g., annual returns), the geometric mean provides the correct average growth factor.
  • Weighted observations: If observations carry different relative importance, the weighted arithmetic mean should be used.
  • Qualitative data: For categorical or ordinal data, the median offers a central position, while the mode identifies the most frequent category; both are preferable to the mean, which lacks interpretability for non‑numeric data.

In practice, no single average fully characterizes a data set. Computing multiple measures—such as the mean, median, and mode—provides a more comprehensive description of the distribution’s central tendency and dispersion.

2.19 central tendencyयों का कौन सा माप कब चुनना है

central tendency के प्रत्येक माप में अलग-अलग ताकत और सीमाएँ होती हैं; resultस्वरूप, उचित average का चुनाव data की attributes और analytical उद्देश्य पर निर्भर करता है। निम्नलिखित दिशानिर्देश उपयुक्त average चुनने में सहायता करते हैं:

  • सममित distribution: जब frequency distribution मोटे तौर पर सममित होता है, तो mean , median और मोड लगभग बराबर होते हैं। ऐसे मामलों में, अंकmathematical mean को उसके वांछनीय mathematical attributeों (example के लिए, रैखिकता, बीजmathematical हेरफेर) के कारण primaryता दी जाती है।
  • विषम distribution: स्पष्ट रूप से तिरछे data के लिए, mean (आउटलेर्स के लिए मजबूत) या मोड (सबसे लगातार value इंगित करता है) mean से अधिक प्रतिनिधि सारांश provide करता है।
  • ओपन-एंडेड वर्ग अंतराल: जब data में ओपन-एंडेड (अनबाउंड) वर्ग होते हैं, तो मध्यिका को आम तौर पर पसंद किया जाता है क्योंकि इसके लिए variableम values के ज्ञान की आवश्यकता नहीं होती है।
  • केवल कुल उपलब्ध हैं: यदि provide की गई एकमात्र information कुल योग और टिप्पणियों की संख्या है, तो अंकmathematical mean एकमात्र व्यवहार्य average है।
  • average अनुपात या परिवर्तन की दरें: ज्यामितीय mean theoretical रूप से विकास दर, सूचकांक संख्या या अनुपात जैसी qualitative मात्राओं के लिए इष्टतम है। जब अंश को स्थिर रखा जाता है (जैसे, गति, यात्रा समय), तो हार्मोनिक mean अधिक उपयुक्त होता है।
  • विषम data के लिए अनुभवजन्य association: जब mean अनुपयुक्त हो और अन्य averageों की गणना करना कठिन हो, तो अनुभवजन्य सन्निकटन mean-मोड≈3(mean-median) एक मोटे समायोजन के रूप में नियोजित किया जा सकता है।
  • विविध वस्तुओं का value निर्धारण: अलग-अलग वस्तुओं (जैसे, फर्नीvariable , उपकरण) की कुल कीमतों के लिए, मोड अक्सर सबसे सामान्य value level को दर्शाता है और average से अधिक informationपूर्ण हो सकता है।
  • परिवर्तन की समान अवधि दरें: जब दरों को समान समय अंतराल (example के लिए, वार्षिक रिटर्न) पर मापा जाता है, तो ज्यामितीय mean सही average वृद्धि कारक provide करता है।
  • भारित टिप्पणियाँ: यदि observation अलग-अलग सापेक्ष महत्व रखते हैं, तो भारित अंकmathematical mean का उपयोग किया जाना चाहिए।
  • qualitative data: श्रेणीबद्ध या क्रमिक data के लिए, median एक केंद्रीय स्थिति provide करती है, जबकि मोड सबसे अधिक बार होने वाली श्रेणी की पहचान करता है; दोनों mean के लिए बेहतर हैं, जिसमें गैर-संख्यात्मक data के लिए व्याख्या की कमी है।

व्यवहार में, कोई भी average किसी data सेट को पूरी तरह से चित्रित नहीं करता है। कई मापों की गणना करना - जैसे कि mean , median और मोड - distribution की central tendency और फैलाव का अधिक व्यापक विवरण provide करता है।

2.20 PARTITION VALUES

Partition values are points that divide a data set or statistical distribution into equal portions. The most common partition values are the median, quartiles, deciles, and percentiles.

3.12.1 Median

The median is the observation that separates the ordered data into two halves; 50% of the observations are ≤median and 50% are ≥median.

3.12.2 Quartiles

Quartiles split the data into four equal parts.

  • First quartile\(Q_{1}\): the value below which 25% of the observations lie.
  • Second quartile\(Q_{2}\): identical to the median (50%).
  • Third quartile\(Q_{3}\): the value below which 75% of the observations lie.

3.12.3 Deciles

Deciles partition the data into ten equal segments.

  • First decile\(D_{1}\): 10% of observations are ≤\(D_{1}\).
  • Second decile\(D_{2}\): 20% of observations are ≤\(D_{2}\).
  • ⋮
  • Fifth decile\(D_{5}\): coincides with the median (50%).
  • ⋮
  • Tenth decile\(D_{10}\): the maximum observation.

3.12.4 Percentiles

Percentiles divide the data into one hundred equal parts.

  • First percentile\(P_{1}\): 1% of observations are ≤\(P_{1}\).
  • Second percentile\(P_{2}\): 2% of observations are ≤\(P_{2}\).
  • ⋮
  • Fiftieth percentile\(P_{50}\): identical to the median (50%).
  • ⋮
  • Hundredth percentile\(P_{100}\): the greatest observation.

All partition values are calculated in the same way as the median: one determines the ordered data, computes the cumulative frequencies, and locates the value at which the required cumulative proportion (\(\frac{k}{m}\), where \(k\) is the desired part and \(m\)=2,4,10, or100) is attained. When the required proportion falls between two observed values, linear interpolation within the containing class (for grouped data) provides an estimate of the partition value.

2.20 विभाजन मान

विभाजन मान वे बिंदु हैं जो data सेट या statistical distribution को समान भागों में विभाजित करते हैं। सबसे सामान्य विभाजन मान median , चतुर्थक, दशमांश और प्रतिशतक हैं।

3.12.1 median

median वह observation है जो क्रमित data को दो हिस्सों में अलग करता है; 50% प्रेक्षण ≤median हैं और 50% प्रेक्षण ≥median हैं।

3.12.2 चतुर्थक

चतुर्थक data को चार बराबर भागों में विभाजित करता है।

  • First quartile\(Q_{1}\): वह मान जिसके नीचे 25% observation स्थित हैं।
  • Second quartile\(Q_{2}\): median के समान (50%)।
  • Third quartile\(Q_{3}\): वह मान जिसके नीचे 75% observation स्थित हैं।

3.12.3 डेसीले

डेसील्स data को दस बराबर खंडों में विभाजित करता है।

  • First decile\(D_{1}\): 10% of observations are ≤\(D_{1}\).
  • Second decile\(D_{2}\): 20% of observations are ≤\(D_{2}\).
  • ⋮
  • Fifth decile\(D_{5}\): median (50%) के साथ मेल खाता है।
  • ⋮
  • Tenth decile\(D_{10}\): अधिकतम observation .

3.12.4 प्रतिशतक

प्रतिशतक data को एक सौ बराबर भागों में विभाजित करते हैं।

  • First percentile\(P_{1}\): 1% of observations are ≤\(P_{1}\).
  • Second percentile\(P_{2}\): 2% of observations are ≤\(P_{2}\).
  • ⋮
  • Fiftieth percentile\(P_{50}\): median के समान (50%)।
  • ⋮
  • Hundredth percentile\(P_{100}\): सबसे बड़ा observation .

All partition values are calculated in the same way as the median: one determines the ordered data, computes the cumulative frequencies, and locates the value at which the required cumulative proportion (\(\frac{k}{m}\), where \(k\) is the desired part and \(m\)=2,4,10, or100) is attained. When the required proportion falls between two observed values, linear interpolation within the containing class (for grouped data) provides an estimate of the partition value.

2.21 Applications of Partition Values

Partition values have numerous applications in statistical analysis, including the following:

  • Assessing distribution shape: By comparing the distances between successive quartiles (e.g., \(Q_{1}, Q_{2}, Q_{3}\)), one can infer whether the distribution is symmetric, skewed, or has heavy tails.
  • Estimating the proportion of observations within a range: If \(Q_{1}=20\) and \(Q_{3}=60\), then 50 % of the data lie between 20 and 60, because the inter‑quartile range always contains the middle half of the observations.
  • Defining measures of dispersion:
    • Inter‑quartile range (IQR): \(IQR = Q_{3} - Q_{1}\)
    • Semi‑inter‑quartile range: \(\frac{IQR}{2}\)
    • Percentile coefficient of dispersion: \(\frac{P_{90} - P_{10}}{P_{90} + P_{10}}\)
  • Quantifying skewness: Bowley’s coefficient of skewness uses quartiles:
    \[ \text{Skewness}_{\text{Bowley}} = \frac{(Q_{3}+Q_{1}-2Q_{2})}{Q_{3}-Q_{1}} \]
  • Interpolation and extrapolation in cumulative frequency distributions: Partition values serve as reference points for estimating intermediate frequencies or extending the distribution beyond observed data.
  • Testing normality: Comparing empirical quartiles or deciles with their theoretical counterparts under a normal distribution (e.g., via a Q‑Q plot) helps assess whether the data follow a normal pattern.
  • Interpreting test scores in educational statistics: Percentile ranks (e.g., a student at the 85th percentile) provide a relative standing of an individual’s performance within a reference group.

Example 3.15a: Results of a Crop Yield Survey

In a crop yield survey, the yield (in quintals per acre) ranged from 5 to 25. The median yield was 15, the first quartile was 10, and the third quartile was 20. Answer the following questions:

  1. What percentage of fields had a yield less than 10 quintals?
  2. What percentage of fields had a yield between 10 and 15 quintals?
  3. What percentage of fields had a yield between 15 and 20 quintals?
  4. What percentage of fields had a yield greater than 20 quintals?
  5. If the survey included 500 fields, how many fields had a yield greater than 20 quintals?

Solution:

  1. The first quartile (\(Q_1\)) is the yield below which 25% of the fields have yield. Therefore, 25% of the fields had a yield less than 10 quintals.
  2. The median (\(Q_2\)) is the yield below which 50% of the fields have yield. Therefore, 50% - 25% = 25% of the fields had a yield between 10 and 15 quintals.
  3. The third quartile (\(Q_3\)) is the yield below which 75% of the fields have yield. Therefore, 75% - 50% = 25% of the fields had a yield between 15 and 20 quintals.
  4. 100% - 75% = 25% of the fields had a yield greater than 20 quintals.
  5. 25% of 500 = 125 fields had a yield greater than 20 quintals.

Example 3.15b: Monthly Agricultural Income of Rural Households

In a rural income survey, the monthly agricultural income (in thousand rupees) of households ranged from 5 to 50. The median income was 25, the first quartile was 15, and the third quartile was 35. Answer the following questions:

  1. What percentage of households had an income less than 15 thousand rupees?
  2. What percentage of households had an income between 15 and 25 thousand rupees?
  3. What percentage of households had an income between 25 and 35 thousand rupees?
  4. What percentage of households had an income greater than 35 thousand rupees?
  5. If the survey included 800 households, how many households had an income greater than 35 thousand rupees?

Solution:

  1. The first quartile (\(Q_1\)) is the income below which 25% of the households have income. Therefore, 25% of the households had an income less than 15 thousand rupees.
  2. The median (\(Q_2\)) is the income below which 50% of the households have income. Therefore, 50% - 25% = 25% of the households had an income between 15 and 25 thousand rupees.
  3. The third quartile (\(Q_3\)) is the income below which 75% of the households have income. Therefore, 75% - 50% = 25% of the households had an income between 25 and 35 thousand rupees.
  4. 100% - 75% = 25% of the households had an income greater than 35 thousand rupees.
  5. 25% of 800 = 200 households had an income greater than 35 thousand rupees.

2.21 विभाजन values के application

statistical analysis में विभाजन values के कई application हैं, जिनमें निम्नलिखित शामिल हैं:

  • distribution size का आकलन: By comparing the distances between successive quartiles (e.g., \(Q_{1}, Q_{2}, Q_{3}\)), one can infer whether the distribution is symmetric, skewed, or has heavy tails.
  • किसी सीमा के भीतर प्रेक्षणों के अनुपात का estimation लगाना: If \(Q_{1}=20\) and \(Q_{3}=60\), then 50 % of the data lie between 20 and 60, because the inter‑quartile range always contains the middle half of the observations.
  • फैलाव के माप को परिभाषित करना:
    • Inter‑quartile range (IQR): \(IQR = Q_{3} - Q_{1}\)
    • Semi‑inter‑quartile range: \(\frac{IQR}{2}\)
    • Percentile coefficient of dispersion: \(\frac{P_{90} - P_{10}}{P_{90} + P_{10}}\)
  • quantitative skewness: बाउली का तिरछापन coefficient चतुर्थक का उपयोग करता है:
    \[ \text{Skewness}_{\text{Bowley}} = \frac{(Q_{3}+Q_{1}-2Q_{2})}{Q_{3}-Q_{1}} \]
  • संचयी frequency distribution में प्रक्षेप और एक्सट्रपलेशन: विभाजन मान मध्यवर्ती frequencyयों का estimation लगाने या प्रेक्षित data से परे distribution का विस्तार करने के लिए संदर्भ बिंदु के रूप में कार्य करते हैं।
  • testing सामान्यता: सामान्य distribution के तहत अनुभवजन्य चतुर्थक या दशमांश की उनके theoretical समकक्षों के साथ तुलना करने से (example के लिए, Q‑Q प्लॉट के meanम से) यह आकलन करने में मदद मिलती है कि data सामान्य पैटर्न का पालन करता है या नहीं।
  • शैक्षिक Statistics में testing अंकों की व्याख्या करना: परसेंटाइल रैंक (example के लिए, 85वें परसेंटाइल पर एक छात्र) एक संदर्भ समूह के भीतर किसी व्यक्ति के प्रदर्शन की सापेक्ष स्थिति provide करता है।

example 3.15ए: फसल yield survey के result

एक फसल yield survey में, yield (प्रति एकड़ क्विंटल में) 5 से 25 के बीच थी। average yield 15 थी, पहला चतुर्थक 10 था, और तीसरा चतुर्थक 20 था। निम्नलिखित प्रश्नों के उत्तर दें:

  1. कितने प्रतिशत खेतों की yield 10 क्विंटल से कम थी?
  2. कितने प्रतिशत खेतों में yield 10 से 15 क्विंटल के बीच थी?
  3. कितने प्रतिशत खेतों में yield 15 से 20 क्विंटल के बीच थी?
  4. कितने प्रतिशत खेतों में yield 20 क्विंटल से अधिक थी?
  5. यदि survey में 500 खेत शामिल थे, तो कितने खेतों की yield 20 क्विंटल से अधिक थी?

solution:

  1. The first quartile (\(Q_1\)) is the yield below which 25% of the fields have yield. Therefore, 25% of the fields had a yield less than 10 quintals.
  2. The median (\(Q_2\)) is the yield below which 50% of the fields have yield. Therefore, 50% - 25% = 25% of the fields had a yield between 10 and 15 quintals.
  3. The third quartile (\(Q_3\)) is the yield below which 75% of the fields have yield. Therefore, 75% - 50% = 25% of the fields had a yield between 15 and 20 quintals.
  4. 100% - 75% = 25% खेतों की yield 20 क्विंटल से अधिक थी।
  5. 500 का 25% = 125 खेतों की yield 20 क्विंटल से अधिक थी।

example 3.15बी: ग्रामीण परिवारों की मासिक कृषि आय

एक ग्रामीण आय survey में, परिवारों की मासिक कृषि आय (हजार रुपये में) 5 से 50 के बीच थी। average आय 25 थी, पहली चतुर्थक 15 थी, और तीसरी चतुर्थक 35 थी। निम्नलिखित प्रश्नों के उत्तर दें:

  1. कितने प्रतिशत परिवारों की आय 15 हजार रुपये से कम थी?
  2. कितने प्रतिशत परिवारों की आय 15 से 25 हजार रुपये के बीच थी?
  3. कितने प्रतिशत परिवारों की आय 25 से 35 हजार रुपये के बीच थी?
  4. कितने प्रतिशत परिवारों की आय 35 हजार रुपये से अधिक थी?
  5. यदि survey में 800 परिवार शामिल थे, तो कितने परिवारों की आय 35 हजार रुपये से अधिक थी?

solution:

  1. The first quartile (\(Q_1\)) is the income below which 25% of the households have income. Therefore, 25% of the households had an income less than 15 thousand rupees.
  2. The median (\(Q_2\)) is the income below which 50% of the households have income. Therefore, 50% - 25% = 25% of the households had an income between 15 and 25 thousand rupees.
  3. The third quartile (\(Q_3\)) is the income below which 75% of the households have income. Therefore, 75% - 50% = 25% of the households had an income between 25 and 35 thousand rupees.
  4. 100% - 75% = 25% परिवारों की आय 35 हजार रुपये से अधिक थी।
  5. 800 में से 25% = 200 परिवारों की आय 35 हजार रुपये से अधिक थी।

2.22 SUMMARY

  • An average is a single numerical summary that represents a collection of data points. Five common types of averages are:
    • Arithmetic mean
    • Geometric mean
    • Harmonic mean
    • Median
    • Mode
  • The arithmetic mean (or simply the mean) of \(n\) observations \(\{x_{1},\dots ,x_{n}\}\) is obtained by dividing the sum of the observations by \(n\):
    \[ \text{Mean} = \frac{x_{1}+x_{2}+\dots +x_{n}}{n}. \]
  • The geometric mean of \(n\) positive values is the \(n\)-th root of their product:
    \[ \text{Geometric Mean} = \bigl(x_{1}\,x_{2}\,\dots \,x_{n}\bigr)^{1/n}. \]
  • The harmonic mean of \(n\) values is the reciprocal of the arithmetic mean of the reciprocals:
    \[ \text{Harmonic Mean} = \frac{n}{\displaystyle\frac{1}{x_{1}}+\frac{1}{x_{2}}+\dots +\frac{1}{x_{n}}}. \]
  • The median of ordered observations is the middle observation when \(n\) is odd; if \(n\) is even, it is the average of the two central observations.
  • The mode is the value that occurs most frequently in a data set; a distribution may be unimodal, bimodal, or multimodal.
  • For moderately asymmetrical distributions the empirical relationship among mean, median, and mode may be approximated by:
    \[ \text{Mode} \approx 3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean}). \]
  • Each average has specific merits and limitations, making it appropriate for particular data structures and analytical objectives.
  • Partition values divide a data set into equal parts; common examples are the median, quartiles, deciles, and percentiles.
  • Applications of partition values in statistical analysis include:
    • Assessing distribution shape by examining distances between quartiles.
    • Estimating the proportion of items within a specified range (e.g., the inter‑quartile range contains 50 % of observations).
    • Constructing measures of dispersion such as the inter‑quartile range, semi‑inter‑quartile range, and percentile coefficient of dispersion.
    • Evaluating skewness via Bowley’s coefficient of skewness that employs quartiles.
    • Performing interpolation and extrapolation in cumulative‑frequency distributions.

2.22 सारांश

  • average एक एकल संख्यात्मक सारांश है जो data बिंदुओं के संग्रह का प्रतिनिधित्व करता है। average के पाँच सामान्य प्रकार हैं:
    • अंकmathematics average
    • ज्यामितीय mean
    • अनुकूल mean
    • मंझला
    • तरीका
  • अंकmathematics average (or simply the mean) of \(n\) observations \(\{x_{1},\dots ,x_{n}\}\) is obtained by dividing the sum of the observations by \(n\):
    \[ \text{Mean} = \frac{x_{1}+x_{2}+\dots +x_{n}}{n}. \]
  • ज्यामितीय mean of \(n\) positive values is the \(n\)-th root of their product:
    \[ \text{Geometric Mean} = \bigl(x_{1}\,x_{2}\,\dots \,x_{n}\bigr)^{1/n}. \]
  • अनुकूल mean of \(n\) values is the reciprocal of the arithmetic mean of the reciprocals:
    \[ \text{Harmonic Mean} = \frac{n}{\displaystyle\frac{1}{x_{1}}+\frac{1}{x_{2}}+\dots +\frac{1}{x_{n}}}. \]
  • MEDIAN of ordered observations is the middle observation when \(n\) is odd; if \(n\) is even, it is the average of the two central observations.
  • तरीका वह मान है जो data सेट में सबसे अधिक बार होता है; एक distribution यूनिmodel , बाइmodel या मल्टीmodel हो सकता है।
  • मध्यम असममित distribution के लिए mean , median और मोड के बीच अनुभवजन्य association का estimation लगाया जा सकता है:
    \[ \text{Mode} \approx 3(\text{Median}) - 2(\text{Mean}). \]
  • प्रत्येक average में विशिष्ट attribute और सीमाएँ होती हैं, जो इसे विशेष data संरचनाओं और analytical उद्देश्यों के लिए उपयुक्त बनाती हैं।
  • विभाजन मान data सेट को समान भागों में विभाजित करते हैं; सामान्य example median , चतुर्थक, दशमांश और शतमक हैं।
  • statistical analysis में विभाजन values के applicationों में शामिल हैं:
    • चतुर्थक के बीच की दूरी की जांच करके distribution size का आकलन करना।
    • एक निर्दिष्ट सीमा के भीतर वस्तुओं के अनुपात का estimation लगाना (example के लिए, अंतर-चतुर्थक सीमा में 50% observation शामिल हैं)।
    • अंतर-चतुर्थक सीमा, अर्ध-अंतर-चतुर्थक सीमा, और फैलाव के प्रतिशतक coefficient जैसे फैलाव के उपायों का निर्माण करना।
    • बाउले के तिरछापन coefficient के meanम से तिरछापन का evaluation करना जो चतुर्थक को नियोजित करता है।
    • संचयी-frequency distribution में प्रक्षेप और एक्सट्रपलेशन करना।

Q1. The process of arranging data in rows and columns is called:

Answer: (b) Tabulation

Answer: (a) Bar chart

(a) Ungrouped data    (b) Grouped frequency distribution    (c) Time series data    (d) Qualitative data

Q4. The most common measure of central tendency is:

(a) Median    (b) Mode    (c) Arithmetic Mean    (d) Geometric Mean

Answer: (c) Arithmetic Mean
Q5. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme values?

(a) Median    (b) Mode    (c) Arithmetic Mean    (d) Geometric Mean

Answer: (c) Arithmetic Mean

(a) Mean    (b) Median    (c) Mode    (d) Harmonic Mean

Answer: (b) Median

(a) Mean    (b) Median    (c) Mode    (d) Average

Answer: (c) Mode
Q8. Geometric Mean is particularly useful for:

(a) Finding average speed    (b) Finding average growth rate    (c) Finding extreme values    (d) Categorical data

Answer: (b) Finding average growth rate

(a) Heights    (b) Weights    (c) Rates and ratios like speed    (d) Income

Answer: (c) Rates and ratios like speed

Answer: (b) 10

Answer: (b) Median

✏️ Fill in the Blanks — 30 Questions

Q1. Arranging data into homogeneous groups based on common characteristics is called ____.
Answer: Classification
Q2. A systematic presentation of numerical data in rows and columns is called ____.
Answer: Tabulation
Q3. The difference between the upper and lower class boundaries is known as class ____.
Answer: Width (or Interval)
Q4. The midpoint of a class is known as the class ____.
Answer: Mark
Q5. A ____ chart represents data using rectangles of equal width but varying heights.
Answer: Bar
Q6. A ____ diagram uses sectors of a circle to represent the components of a total.
Answer: Pie
Q7. The graphical representation of a grouped frequency distribution using contiguous rectangles is a ____.
Answer: Histogram
Q8. An Ogive is plotted using ____ frequencies.
Answer: Cumulative
Q9. The measure of central tendency defined as the sum of all observations divided by the number of observations is the ____.
Answer: Arithmetic Mean
Q10. The middlemost value in an ordered dataset is the ____.
Answer: Median
Q11. The value that occurs most frequently in a dataset is called the ____.
Answer: Mode
Q12. The nth root of the product of n observations is called the ____ Mean.
Answer: Geometric
Q13. The reciprocal of the arithmetic mean of the reciprocals of observations is the ____ Mean.
Answer: Harmonic
Q14. For averaging rates and speeds, the appropriate measure is the ____ Mean.
Answer: Harmonic
Q15. The sum of deviations of individual items from their arithmetic mean is always ____.
Answer: Zero
Q16. Values that divide a dataset into four equal parts are called ____.
Answer: Quartiles
Q17. Values that divide a dataset into ten equal parts are called ____.
Answer: Deciles
Q18. The Second Quartile (Q2) is equal to the ____.
Answer: Median
Q19. The ____ decile is equal to the median.
Answer: 5th (Fifth)
Q20. The ____ percentile is equal to the Third Quartile (Q3).
Answer: 75th
Q21. In a positively skewed distribution, the Mean is ____ than the Median.
Answer: Greater
Q22. The empirical formula connecting mean, median, and mode is Mode = 3 ____ - 2 Mean.
Answer: Median
Q23. A frequency polygon is obtained by joining the midpoints of the tops of the rectangles in a ____.
Answer: Histogram
Q24. Stem-and-leaf display retains the original ____ while grouping them.
Answer: Values (or Data)
Q25. For averaging growth rates or percentages, the ____ Mean is best.
Answer: Geometric
Q26. Extreme values strongly affect the ____.
Answer: Arithmetic Mean
Q27. If a dataset has two values with the highest identical frequency, it is called ____.
Answer: Bimodal
Q28. The number of observations falling in a particular class is called the class ____.
Answer: Frequency
Q29. A table has rows and ____.
Answer: Columns
Q30. The intersection of an Ogive 'less than' and Ogive 'more than' gives the ____.
Answer: Median
